## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly suggests a constitutive law for a material under mechanical loading with temperature-dependent stiffness/yield/softening. Common relationships include linear/nonlinear elasticity, thermoelastic strain offsets (thermal expansion), and temperature-dependent plastic hardening/softening forms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changes with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (quadratic-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (curved E(T) behavior over wider T range)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain)
- Thermoelastic with E(T) and thermal strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (combined temperature effects on stiffness and expansion)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain nonlinear elasticity)
- Exponential stiffening/softening in strain: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (rubbery/soft polymer-like nonlinear response)
- Power-law strain hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (plastic hardening beyond yield with curvature control)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening that approaches a saturation stress)
- Rational hardening/softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (epsilon + c1) (rapid initial increase then gradual saturation with strain)
- Multiplicative thermal softening factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)**c5 (strength decreases/increases systematically with temperature)
- Yield-like transition smoothed in strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * tanh(c2 * (epsilon - c3)) (captures a knee/transition from elastic to post-yield response)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma proportional to epsilon implies a linear modulus; departures suggest nonlinear elasticity or onset of plasticity.
- Thermal expansion manifests as a strain shift: forms like (epsilon - c*(T - c0)) indicate that stress depends on mechanical strain relative to a temperature-dependent free strain.
- Temperature-dependent stiffness is often separable: sigma ≈ E(T) * epsilon, where E(T) is commonly linear/quadratic over moderate temperature ranges and drops rapidly near transitions.
- Post-yield hardening curvature: power laws in epsilon (epsilon**n) indicate continuous work hardening; the exponent controls concavity/convexity of sigma–epsilon.
- Hardening saturation behavior: (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or epsilon/(epsilon+c) patterns imply approach to a limiting stress with increasing strain.
- Thermal softening often acts multiplicatively on strength: (strength in epsilon) * g(T) captures reduced flow stress at higher T without changing the basic hardening shape.
- Yield/transition smoothing: tanh(c*(epsilon-c0)) (or similar sigmoids) captures a knee without explicit piecewise definitions, approximating elastic-to-plastic transition.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity: cross terms like T*epsilon or (c0+c1*T)*(epsilon-c2*(T-c3)) indicate that temperature changes both the slope and the strain offset of the stress–strain curve.

\[
5.889184448896621\,\epsilon^{3}\;+\;2.8821771197066277\,(T-279.6235977851866)\,\sin(\epsilon)
\]
So GT has exactly:
- a pure \(\epsilon^3\) term with constant coefficient (independent of \(T\)),
- plus a \(\sin(\epsilon)\) term whose amplitude is **affine in \(T\)**: \(2.8821771\,T - 2.8821771\cdot 279.6236\),
- and **no other** dependence on \(\epsilon\) (no \(\epsilon^2,\epsilon,\) constants, exp/log/cos terms, etc.).

For a candidate to match, it must be able (by parameter choices) to reduce *exactly* to “constant\(\cdot \epsilon^3\) + (aT+b)\sin(\epsilon)”.

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*sin(epsilon)

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: 5.889*epsilon³ + 2.882*(T - 279.624)*sin(epsilon)**

This expands to: **5.889*epsilon³ + 2.882*T*sin(epsilon) - 806.098*sin(epsilon)**

The GT has three basis function components:
1. **epsilon³** (a cubic term in epsilon)
2. **T*sin(epsilon)** (T times sin of epsilon)
3. **sin(epsilon)** (standalone sin of epsilon)

Let me analyze each candidate:

### Candidate 1: T*c0*(c1+epsilon)² + T*c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon² + c5*epsilon + c6*exp(c7*cos(c8*exp(c9*epsilon)))
Expanding T*c0*(c1+epsilon)² = T*c0*c1² + 2*T*c0*c1*epsilon + T*c0*epsilon²
This gives polynomial terms in T and epsilon, plus an exponential-cosine-exponential term. No epsilon³ term, no sin(epsilon). The exp(cos(exp)) term cannot produce both epsilon³ and sin(epsilon).
**Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: c0*epsilon² + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*exp(T*c4*epsilon) + c5*sin(c6*epsilon + c7)
The exp(T*c4*epsilon) term couples T and epsilon exponentially - cannot match T*sin(epsilon). Setting c4=0 kills the T dependence entirely. The sin term has no T dependence.
**Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: T*c0*(c1+epsilon)² + c2*epsilon² + c3*epsilon + c4 + c5*exp(c6*cos(c7*exp(c8*epsilon))) + c9*epsilon³
Expanding: T*c0*c1² + 2*T*c0*c1*epsilon + T*c0*epsilon² + c2*epsilon² + c3*epsilon + c4 + c5*exp(c6*cos(c7*exp(c8*epsilon))) + c9*epsilon³
This has c9*epsilon³ (good!), but T dependence is polynomial in epsilon (T*epsilon², T*epsilon, T). We need T*sin(epsilon). The exp(cos(exp)) term doesn't depend on T. Cannot produce T*sin(epsilon).
**Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 4: Similar to Candidate 3 but without epsilon³ explicitly. Same issue - no T*sin(epsilon).
**Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 5: Same structure issue as 3/4.
**Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 6: T²*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon + c2*exp(c3*|epsilon|) + c4*epsilon + c5 + c6*exp(T*c7)*sin(c8*epsilon + c9)
The term c6*exp(T*c7)*sin(c8*epsilon+c9): if c7=0, this becomes c6*sin(c8*epsilon+c9), losing T dependence. We need T*sin(epsilon), but exp(T*c7) ≠ T for any constant c7. Cannot match.
**Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 7: c0*epsilon² + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*exp(T*c4*epsilon) + c5*sin(c6*epsilon+c7)*cos(T*c8)
For T*sin(epsilon): cos(T*c8) doesn't give T dependence linearly. Setting c4=0 kills exp term's T dependence. Cannot produce T*sin(epsilon).
**Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 8: No T*sin(epsilon) possible.
**Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 9: T*(c0+epsilon)² + c1*epsilon² + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*exp(c5*cos(c6*exp(c7*epsilon)))
= T*c0² + 2*T*c0*epsilon + T*epsilon² + ... No T*sin(epsilon).
**Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

GT needs: epsilon³ + T*sin(epsilon) terms + sin(epsilon) terms.

We need epsilon³ from the remaining terms: c7*epsilon + c8/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c0*epsilon + T*c1/(c2*epsilon+c3).

The non-T terms are c7*epsilon + c8/(c2*epsilon+c3). These cannot produce epsilon³.

We also need a standalone sin(epsilon) term (from -c3*c2 in GT). The candidate has no standalone sin term (the sin is multiplied by T).
